https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\\n413: \\t\\t\\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\\n414: \\t\\t\\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\\n415: \\t\\t\\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\\n416: \\t\\t\\t//\\n417: \\t\\t\\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\\n418: \\t\\t\\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\\n419: \\t\\t\\t// unschedulable pod pool.\\n420: \\t\\t\\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\\n421: \\t\\t\\t// See: \\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\\n438: \\n439: \\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\\n440: \\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\\n441: \\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\\n442: \\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\\n443: \\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\\n444: \\t// \\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Run(logger)\\n438: \\n439: \\t// We need to start scheduleOne loop in a dedicated goroutine,\\n440: \\t// because scheduleOne function hangs on getting the next item\\n441: \\t// from the SchedulingQueue.\\n442: \\t// If there are no new pods to schedule, it will be hanging there\\n443: \\t// and if done in this goroutine it will be blocking closing\\n444: \\t// }\n371: \n372: func buildQueueingHintMap(es []framework.EnqueueExtensions) internalqueue.QueueingHintMap {\n373: \tqueueingHintMap := make(internalqueue.QueueingHintMap)\n374: \tfor _, e := range es {\n375: \t\tevents := e.EventsToRegister()\n376: \n377: \t\t// This will happen when plugin registers with empty events, it's usually the case a pod\n378: \t\t// will become reschedulable only for self-update, e.g. schedulingGates plugin, the pod\n379: \t\t// will enter into the activeQ via priorityQueue.Update().\n380: \t\tif len(events) == 0 {\n381: \t\t\tcontinue\n382: \t\t}\n383: \n384: \t\t// Note: Rarely, a plugin implements EnqueueExtensions but returns nil.\n385: \t\t// We treat it as: the plugin is not interested in any event, and hence pod failed by that plugin\n386: \t\t// cannot be moved by any regular cluster event.\n387: \t\t// So, we can just ignore such EventsToRegister here.\n388: \n389: \t\tregisterNodeAdded := false\n390: \t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated := false\n391: \t\tfor _, event := range events {\n392: \t\t\tfn := event.QueueingHintFn\n393: \t\t\tif fn == nil || !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.SchedulerQueueingHints) {\n394: \t\t\t\tfn = defaultQueueingHintFn\n395: \t\t\t}\n396: \n397: \t\t\tif event.Event.Resource == framework.Node {\n398: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.Add != 0 {\n399: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeAdded = true\n400: \t\t\t\t}\n401: \t\t\t\tif event.Event.ActionType&framework.UpdateNodeTaint != 0 {\n402: \t\t\t\t\tregisterNodeTaintUpdated = true\n403: \t\t\t\t}\n404: \t\t\t}\n405: \n406: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[event.Event] = append(queueingHintMap[event.Event], &internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n407: \t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n408: \t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: fn,\n409: \t\t\t})\n410: \t\t}\n411: \t\tif registerNodeAdded && !registerNodeTaintUpdated {\n412: \t\t\t// Temporally fix for the issue https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/109437\n413: \t\t\t// NodeAdded QueueingHint isn't always called because of preCheck.\n414: \t\t\t// It's definitely not something expected for plugin developers,\n415: \t\t\t// and registering UpdateNodeTaint event is the only mitigation for now.\n416: \t\t\t//\n417: \t\t\t// So, here registers UpdateNodeTaint event for plugins that has NodeAdded event, but don't have UpdateNodeTaint event.\n418: \t\t\t// It has a bad impact for the requeuing efficiency though, a lot better than some Pods being stuch in the\n419: \t\t\t// unschedulable pod pool.\n420: \t\t\t// This behavior will be removed when we remove the preCheck feature.\n421: \t\t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n422: \t\t\tqueueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}] =\n423: \t\t\t\tappend(queueingHintMap[framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.UpdateNodeTaint}],\n424: \t\t\t\t\t&internalqueue.QueueingHintFunction{\n425: \t\t\t\t\t\tPluginName:     e.Name(),\n426: \t\t\t\t\t\tQueueingHintFn: defaultQueueingHintFn,\n427: framework.AsStatus(err)\\n206: \\t}\\n207: \\n208: \\t// Run the Reserve method of reserve plugins.\\n209: \\tif sts := fwk.RunReservePluginsReserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost); !sts.IsSuccess() {\\n210: \\t\\t// trigger un-reserve to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\\n211: \\t\\tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\\n212: \\t\\tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\\n213: \\t\\t\\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \\\"Scheduler cache nil\\n262: }\\n263: \\n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\\n266: \\tctx context.Context,\\n267: \\tstate *framework.CycleState,\\n268: {\\n659: \\tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\\n660: \\t\\treturn numAllNodes\\n661: \\t}\\n662: \\n663: \\t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = nil\\n910: }\\n911: \\n912: // nodeScoreHeap is a heap of framework.NodePluginScores.\\n913: type nodeScoreHeap []framework.NodePluginScores\\n914: \\n915: // nodeScoreHeap implements {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons \t\t\t}\n733: \t\t}\n734: \n735: \t\tfeasibleNodes = feasibleList\n736: \t}\n737: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n738: }\n739: \n740: // prioritizeNodes prioritizes the nodes by running the score plugins,\n741: // which return a score for each node from the call to RunScorePlugins().\n742: // The scores from each plugin are added together to make the score for that node, then\n743: // any extenders are run as well.\n744: // All scores are finally combined (added) to get the total weighted scores of all nodes\n745: func prioritizeNodes(\n746: \tctx context.Context,\n747: \textenders []framework.Extender,\n748: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n749: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n750: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n751: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo,\n752: ) ([]framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n753: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n754: \t// If no priority configs are provided, then all nodes will have a score of one.\n755: \t// This is required to generate the priority list in the \t\t\t\tnodesScores[i].TotalScore += score.TotalScore\n845: \t\t\t}\n846: \t\t}\n847: \t}\n848: \n849: \tif loggerVTen.Enabled() {\n850: \t\tfor i := range nodesScores {\n851: \t\t\tloggerVTen.Info(\"Calculated node's final score for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", nodesScores[i].Name, \"score\", nodesScores[i].TotalScore)\n852: \t\t}\n853: \t}\n854: \treturn nodesScores, nil\n855: }\n856: \n857: var errEmptyPriorityList = errors.New(\"empty priorityList\")\n858: \n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\n864: \tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\n865: \t\treturn \"\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\n866: \t}\n867: \n868: \tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\n869: \theap.Init(&h)\n870: \tcntOfMaxScore := 1\n871: \tselectedIndex := 0\n872: \t// The top of the heap is the NodeScoreResult with the highest score.\n873: \tsortedNodeScoreList := make([]framework.NodePluginScores, 0, count)\n874: \tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\n875: \n876: \t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\n877: \t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\n878: \tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores) {\n879: \t\tif ns.TotalScore != sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore && len(sortedNodeScoreList) == count {\n880: \t\t\tbreak\n881: \t\t}\n882: \n883: \t\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\n884: \t\t\tcntOfMaxScore++\n885: \t\t\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\n886: \t\t\t\t// Replace the candidate with probability of 1/cntOfMaxScore\n887: \t\t\t\tselectedIndex = cntOfMaxScore - 1\n888: \t\t\t}\n889: \t\t}\n890: \n891: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, ns)\n892: \n893: \t\tif h.Len() == 0 {\n894: \t\t\tbreak\n895: \t\t}\n896: \t}\n897: \n898: \tif selectedIndex != 0 {\n899: \t\t// replace the first one with selected one\n900: \t\tprevious := sortedNodeScoreList[0]\n901: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList[0] = sortedNodeScoreList[selectedIndex]\n902: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList[selectedIndex] = previous\n903: \t}\n904: \n905: \tif len(sortedNodeScoreList) > count {\n906: \t\tsortedNodeScoreList = sortedNodeScoreList[:count]\n907: \t}\n908: \n909: \treturn sortedNodeScoreList[0].Name, sortedNodeScoreList, nil\n910: }\n911: \n912: // nodeScoreHeap is a heap of framework.NodePluginScores.\n913: type nodeScoreHeap Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable and\\n97: \\t// other postFilter plugins like preemption would not change anything.\\n98: \\t// See the comment on PostFilter interface for more details about how PostFilter should handle this plugins.\\n73: type Code int\\n74: \\n75: // These are predefined codes used in a Status.\\n76: // Note: when you add a new status, you have to add it in `codes` slice below.\\n77: const (\\n78: \\t// Success means that plugin ran correctly and found pod schedulable.\\n79: \\t// NOTE: A nil status is also considered as \\\"Success\\\".\\n80: \\tSuccess Code = iota\\n81: \\t// Error is one of the failures, used for internal plugin errors, unexpected input, etc.\\n82: \\t// Plugin shouldn't return this code for expected failures, like Unschedulable.\\n83: \\t// Since it's the unexpected failure, the scheduling queue registers the pod without unschedulable plugins.\\n84: \\t// Meaning, the Pod will be requeued to activeQ/backoffQ soon.\\n85: \\tError\\n86: \\t// Unschedulable is one of the failures, used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable.\\n87: \\t// If it's returned from PreFilter or Filter, the scheduler might attempt to\\n88: \\t// run other postFilter plugins like preemption to get this pod scheduled.\\n89: \\t// Use UnschedulableAndUnresolvable to make the scheduler skipping other postFilter plugins.\\n90: \\t// The accompanying status message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n91: \\t//\\n92: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n93: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with Unschedulable in the last scheduling,\\n94: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n95: \\tUnschedulable\\n96: \\t// UnschedulableAndUnresolvable is used when a plugin finds a pod unschedulable message should explain why the pod is unschedulable.\\n102: \\t//\\n103: \\t// We regard the backoff as a penalty of wasting the scheduling cycle.\\n104: \\t// When the scheduling queue requeues Pods, which was rejected with UnschedulableAndUnresolvable in the last scheduling,\\n105: \\t// the Pod goes through backoff.\\n106: \\tUnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\n107: \\t// Wait is used when a Permit plugin finds a pod scheduling should wait.\\n108: \\tWait\\n109: \\t// Skip is used in the following scenarios:\\n110: \\t// - when a Bind plugin chooses to skip binding.\\n111: \\t// - when a PreFilter plugin returns Skip so that coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped.\\n112: \\t// - when a PreScore plugin returns Skip so that coupled Score plugin will be skipped.\\n113: \\tSkip\\n114: \\t// Pending means that the scheduling process is finished successfully,\\n115: \\t// but the plugin wants to stop the scheduling cycle/binding cycle here.\\n116: Each event has a callback function that\\n373: \\t// filters out events to reduce useless retry of Pod's scheduling.\\n374: \\t// The events will be registered when instantiating the internal scheduling queue,\\n375: \\t// and leveraged to build event handlers dynamically.\\n376: \\t// Note: the returned list needs to be static (not depend on configuration parameters);\\n377: \\t// otherwise it would lead to undefined behavior.\\n378: \\t//\\n379: \\t// Appropriate implementation of this function will make Pod's re-scheduling accurate and performant.\\n380: \\tEventsToRegister() []ClusterEventWithHint\\n381: }\\n382: \\n383: // PreFilterExtensions is an interface that is included in plugins that allow specifying\\n384: // callbacks to make incremental updates to its supposedly pre-calculated\\n385: // state.\\n386: type PreFilterExtensions interface {\\n387: \\t// AddPod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n388: \\t// of adding podToAdd to the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n389: \\tAddPod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToAdd *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n390: \\t// RemovePod is called by the framework while trying to evaluate the impact\\n391: \\t// of removing podToRemove from the node while scheduling podToSchedule.\\n392: \\tRemovePod(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, podToSchedule *v1.Pod, podInfoToRemove *PodInfo, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n393: }\\n394: \\n395: // PreFilterPlugin is an interface that must be implemented by \\\"PreFilter\\\" plugins.\\n396: // These plugins are called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle.\\n397: type PreFilterPlugin interface {\\n398: \\tPlugin\\n399: \\t// PreFilter is called at the beginning of the scheduling cycle. This is useful\\n402: \\t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\\n403: \\t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\".\\n404: \\t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\\n405: \\t//\\n406: \\t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\\n407: \\t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\\n408: \\tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\\n409: \\t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\\n410: \\t// or nil if it does not. If Filter doesn't return \\\"Success\\\",\\n430: \\t// it will return \\\"Unschedulable\\\", \\\"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\\\" or \\\"Error\\\".\\n431: \\t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\\n432: \\t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\\n433: \\t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\\n434: \\t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\\n435: \\t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\\n436: \\t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\\n437: \\t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\\n438: \\tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\\n439: }\\n440: \\n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \\\"PostFilter\\\" plugins. This is useful\n402: \t// for cases where it is possible to determine the subset of nodes to process in O(1) time.\n403: \t// When PreFilterResult filters out some Nodes, the framework considers Nodes that are filtered out as getting \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\".\n404: \t// i.e., those Nodes will be out of the candidates of the preemption.\n405: \t//\n406: \t// When it returns Skip status, returned PreFilterResult and other fields in status are just ignored,\n407: \t// and coupled Filter plugin/PreFilterExtensions() will be skipped in this scheduling cycle.\n408: \tPreFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, p *v1.Pod) (*PreFilterResult, *Status)\n409: \t// PreFilterExtensions returns a PreFilterExtensions interface if the plugin implements one,\n410: \t// or nil if it does not. If Filter doesn't return \"Success\",\n430: \t// it will return \"Unschedulable\", \"UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\" or \"Error\".\n431: \t// For the node being evaluated, Filter plugins should look at the passed\n432: \t// nodeInfo reference for this particular node's information (e.g., pods\n433: \t// considered to be running on the node) instead of looking it up in the\n434: \t// NodeInfoSnapshot because we don't guarantee that they will be the same.\n435: \t// For example, during preemption, we may pass a copy of the original\n436: \t// nodeInfo object that has some pods removed from it to evaluate the\n437: \t// possibility of preempting them to schedule the target pod.\n438: \tFilter(ctx context.Context, state *CycleState, pod *v1.Pod, nodeInfo *NodeInfo) *Status\n439: }\n440: \n441: // PostFilterPlugin is an interface for \"PostFilter\" plugins. For performance reasons,\\n34: \\t// clone should make shallow copies for members (e.g., slices or maps) that are not\\n35: \\t// impacted by PreFilter's optional AddPod/RemovePod methods.\\n36: \\tClone() StateData\\n37: }\\n38: \\n39: // StateKey is the type of keys stored in CycleState.\\n40: type StateKey string\\n41: \\n42: // CycleState provides a mechanism for plugins to store and retrieve arbitrary data.\\n43: // StateData stored by one plugin can be read, altered, or deleted by another plugin.\\n44: // CycleState does not provide any data protection, as all plugins are assumed to be\\n45: // trusted.\\n46: // Note: CycleState uses a sync.Map to back the storage, because it is thread safe. instantiates plugins and executes them\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/runtime/registry.go** — Plugin registry mapping plugin names to factory functions\n- **pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/** — Built-in plugin implementations (NodeResourcesFit, InterPodAffinity, PodTopologySpread, etc.)\n\n### Scheduling Queue\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go** — SchedulingQueue interface and PriorityQueue implementation with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods sub-queues\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/events.go** — Cluster events and queueing hints for requeuing pods\n\n### Cache\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/cache.go** — Cache struct managing assumed pods, node info, and image states\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/snapshot.go** — Snapshot of cache taken at start of scheduling cycle\n- **pkg/scheduler/internal/cache/node_tree.go** — Efficient node lookup structure\n\n### Profiles\n- **pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go** — Profile struct wrapping a Framework instance for a scheduler profile\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n### 1. Entry Point: Pod Lifecycle\n```\nEvent Source (API Server)\n  ↓\neventhandlers.go: addPodToSchedulingQueue()\n  ↓ (via Informer)\ninternalqueue.SchedulingQueue: Add()\n  ↓\nPod enters activeQ/backoffQ\n```\n\n### 2. Main Scheduling Loop\n```\nScheduler.Run() [pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:435]\n  ↓ (spawns goroutine)\nScheduler.ScheduleOne() [pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go:66]\n  ↓\nScheduler.NextPod() → SchedulingQueue.Pop()\n  ↓ (retrieves next pod from priority queue)\nframework.QueuedPodInfo\n```\n\n### 3. Scheduling Cycle (Lock & Assume Phase)\n```\nScheduler.ScheduleOne() [schedule_one.go:66]\n  ├─ Scheduler.schedulingCycle() [schedule_one.go:139]\n  │   ├─ Scheduler.SchedulePod() [schedule_one.go:390] (delegated to sched.SchedulePod function)\n  │   │   ├─ Cache.UpdateSnapshot() — creates point-in-time snapshot of nodes\n  │   │   ├─ Scheduler.findNodesThatFitPod() [schedule_one.go:442]\n  │   │   │   ├─ Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins()\n  │   │   │   │   ├─ frameworkImpl.runPreFilterPlugin() [runtime/framework.go:700+]\n  │   │   │   │   └─ PreFilterPlugin.PreFilter()\n  │   │   │   ├─ Scheduler.findNodesThatPassFilters()\n  │   │   │   │   ├─ Framework.RunFilterPlugins() [runs in parallel via parallelizer]\n  │   │   │   │   │   └─ FilterPlugin.Filter()\n  │   │   │   │   └─ Returns feasibleNodes list\n  │   │   │   └─ Returns diagnosis with node statuses\n  │   │   ├─ Framework.RunPreScorePlugins()\n  │   │   │   └─ PreScorePlugin.PreScore()\n  │   │   ├─ prioritizeNodes() — scores via Framework.RunScorePlugins()\n  │   │   │   └─ ScorePlugin.Score() + NormalizeScore()\n  │   │   └─ selectHost() — picks best node\n  │   │\n  │   ├─ Scheduler.assume() — marks pod as assumed in cache\n  │   ├─ Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve() — reserve plugins update state\n  │   │   └─ ReservePlugin.Reserve()\n  │   └─ Framework.RunPermitPlugins() — permit plugins can delay/reject\n  │       └─ PermitPlugin.Permit()\n  │\n  └─ Binding Cycle (async via goroutine) [schedule_one.go:118-133]\n      └─ Scheduler.bindingCycle() [schedule_one.go:265]\n          ├─ Framework.WaitOnPermit() — wait for any delayed permits\n          ├─ Framework.RunPreBindPlugins()\n          │   └─ PreBindPlugin.PreBind()\n          ├─ Scheduler.bind() → Framework.RunBindPlugins()\n          │   └─ BindPlugin.Bind() — typically creates pod binding via API\n          ├─ Framework.RunPostBindPlugins()\n          │   └─ PostBindPlugin.PostBind()\n          └─ Cache.ForgetPod() OR Cache.AssumedPods cleanup\n```\n\n### 4. Plugin Framework Initialization\n```\nScheduler.New() [pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go:252]\n  ├─ profile.NewMap() [pkg/scheduler/profile/profile.go]\n  │   └─ frameworkruntime.NewFramework() [framework/runtime/framework.go:242]\n  │       ├─ Registry.Factory() — instantiates each plugin\n  │       │   └─ pluginFactoryFunc(ctx, args, handle)\n  │       ├─ frameworkImpl.getExtensionPoints()\n  │       ├─ updatePluginList() — assigns plugins to extension point lists\n  │       ├─ frameworkImpl.expandMultiPointPlugins()\n  │       └─ frameworkImpl.setInstrumentedPlugins() — wraps with metrics\n  │\n  └─ SchedulingQueue.NewSchedulingQueue() [pkg/scheduler/internal/queue/scheduling_queue.go:130]\n      └─ PriorityQueue with activeQ, backoffQ, unschedulablePods\n```\n\n## Design Patterns & Architecture\n\n### Two-Phase Scheduling Design\n\n**Scheduling Cycle (Synchronous Lock Phase)**\n- Pod is popped from queue and sent through filtering/scoring plugins\n- Framework.RunPreFilterPlugins() → Framework.RunFilterPlugins() → Framework.RunScorePlugins()\n- Best node is selected\n- **\"Assume\" step**: Pod is marked as running on node in cache (pessimistic locking)\n- Framework.RunReservePluginsReserve() allows plugins to reserve resources\n- Framework.RunPermitPlugins() can delay or reject at last moment\n- Returns CycleState with scheduling decision\n\n**Binding Cycle (Asynchronous Unbind Phase)**\n- Runs in separate goroutine (doesn't block scheduler)\n- Framework.WaitOnPermit() blocks if permit plugins requested wait\n- Framework.RunPreBindPlugins() final checks before binding\n- Framework.RunBindPlugins() creates actual Pod-to-Node binding in API server\n- Framework.RunPostBindPlugins() cleanup/notifications\n- If binding fails, assumed pod is \"forgotten\" from cache, triggering requeue\n\n### Plugin Framework Architecture\n\n**Extension Points (Hooks)**\n1. **PreEnqueue** — Filter pods before adding to queue (in-place optimization)\n2. **QueueSort** — Sort pods in scheduling queue (exactly one plugin required)\n3. **PreFilter** — Pre-process pod; may exclude nodes or skip filter phase\n4. **Filter** — Run in parallel; determine feasible nodes (replaces old \"Predicates\")\n5. **PostFilter** — Run if no feasible nodes (e.g., preemption logic)\n6. **PreScore** — Information-only; ran for feasible nodes\n7. **Score** — Run in parallel; score each feasible node (replaces old \"Priorities\")\n8. **Reserve** — Update plugin state after scheduling decision\n9. **Permit** — Final gate before binding; can wait or reject\n10. **PreBind** — Final checks immediately before binding\n11. **Bind** — Perform actual binding (one of plugins in list will bind)\n12. **PostBind** — Cleanup after successful binding\n\n**Plugin Lifecycle**\n- Plugins are loaded from Registry based on KubeSchedulerProfile configuration\n- Each plugin implements framework.Plugin interface (Name() method)\n- Plugins can optionally implement EnqueueExtensions for event-based requeuing\n- frameworkImpl calls pluginFactoryFunc with context, args, and Handle (which provides access to cache, listers, event recorder)\n- Plugins store scheduling-cycle state in CycleState.storage (thread-safe sync.Map)\n\n### Scheduling Queue\n\n**Three-Queue Model**\n- **activeQ** (priority heap): Pods being actively considered for scheduling\n- **backoffQ** (priority heap by backoff expiry): Pods in backoff after failed attempt\n- **unschedulablePods**: Pods determined unschedulable; moved to backoffQ after timeout\n\n**Queueing Hints & Efficient Requeuing**\n- Plugins implement EnqueueExtensions.EventsToRegister() to specify cluster events they care about\n- When event occurs (e.g., node added, taint removed), only affected pods are requeued\n- Avoids requeuing all pods for every cluster event (performance optimization)\n\n### Cache Architecture\n\n**Assumptions & Snapshot Model**\n- When pod is assumed, it's added to cache with nodeName set\n- Real Pod in API server doesn't have nodeName yet (binding hasn't occurred)\n- Cache maintains assumedPods set and podState map tracking assumed pods and their deadlines\n- Deadlines allow cache to clean up stale assumed pods (prevents memory leaks if binding fails)\n\n**Node Information Management**\n- Cache.NodeInfo tracks pods, resources, and predicates on each node\n- Doubly-linked list of NodeInfo sorted by recency (head = most recent)\n- UpdateSnapshot() called at start of scheduling cycle creates point-in-time view\n- Generation numbers track changes, allowing incremental snapshot updates\n\n**Image States**\n- Tracks image pull latency and availability on nodes\n- Used by plugins like ImageLocality for scheduling decisions\n\n### CycleState Design\n\n**Thread-Safe Scheduling Context**\n- Each pod gets its own CycleState instance for a scheduling cycle\n- Backed by sync.Map for \"write once, read many\" optimization\n- Plugins can store intermediate results (e.g., PreFilter stores computed data read by Filter)\n- Allows zero-copy plugin communication\n\n**State Propagation**\n- PodsToActivateKey reserved key: Plugins can inject pods to be activated post-scheduling\n- SkipFilterPlugins, SkipScorePlugins: PreFilter/PreScore plugins can signal to skip coupled plugins\n- Plugin metrics flags: Controls per-cycle metrics recording\n\n### Multi-Profile Support\n\n**Scheduler Profiles**\n- Scheduler can run multiple scheduler profiles simultaneously\n- Each profile has own Framework, QueueSort, and plugin chain\n- Pods specify .spec.schedulerName to choose profile\n- Allows different scheduling logic for different workload types\n\n## Key Data Structures\n\n### ScheduleResult\n```go\ntype ScheduleResult struct {\n    SuggestedHost string           // Selected node name\n    EvaluatedNodes int             // Nodes evaluated in filtering + beyond\n    FeasibleNodes int              // Nodes that passed filtering\n    nominatingInfo *NominatingInfo // For preemption tracking\n}\n```\n\n### QueuedPodInfo\n```go\ntype QueuedPodInfo struct {\n    Pod                      *v1.Pod\n    Timestamp                time.Time     // When pod entered queue\n    UnschedulablePlugins     sets.Set[string]\n    Attempts                 int           // Scheduling attempts count\n    InitialAttemptTimestamp  *time.Time\n}\n```\n\n### FitError (Scheduling Failure)\n```go\ntype FitError struct {\n    Pod         *v1.Pod\n    NumAllNodes int\n    Diagnosis   Diagnosis\n}\n\ntype Diagnosis struct {\n    NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status  // Per-node rejection reasons\n    PreFilterMsg    string\n    PostFilterMsg   string\n}\n```\n\n## Data Flow During Scheduling\n\n1. **Pod Arrival**: Pod added to queue via event handler\n2. **Pop Phase**: ScheduleOne pops next pod from queue\n3. **Framework Selection**: Find Framework matching pod's schedulerName\n4. **Snapshot**: Cache.UpdateSnapshot() creates point-in-time node view\n5. **PreFilter**: Plugins may narrow down candidate nodes\n6. **Filter**: Determine feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n7. **Score**: Rank feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n8. **Selection**: Pick best node\n9. **Assume**: Mark pod as running on node in cache\n10. **Reserve**: Plugins update internal state\n11. **Permit**: Final gate; can delay or reject\n12. **Bind (async)**: Wait for permits, run PreBind plugins, call Bind plugins, run PostBind\n13. **Cleanup**: Mark pod as truly scheduled or requeue if binding failed\n\n## Failure Handling\n\n**Scheduling Cycle Failure** → Handled by FailureHandler\n- PostFilterPlugins run (e.g., preemption to free up resources)\n- Pod moved to backoffQ with exponential backoff\n- Will retry after backoff expires or cluster event occurs\n\n**Binding Cycle Failure** → Handled by handleBindingCycleError\n- Called if PreBind, Bind, or PostBind plugins fail\n- Reserve plugins' Unreserve methods called to clean up\n- assumed pod forgotten from cache\n- Pod requeued (triggers event-based requeue or backoff)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase lock-free scheduling architecture using a plugin framework. Pods are sorted via PriorityQueue, processed through a snapshot of cluster state, evaluated by parallel filter/score plugins, and speculatively assumed to run on selected nodes. The binding phase then asynchronously confirms the scheduling decision. The design enables multiple scheduling profiles, efficient event-driven pod requeuing via queueing hints, and extensibility through plugin interfaces at twelve extension points. CycleState provides thread-safe temporary state sharing between plugins, while the cache maintains node information with generation tracking for efficient incremental snapshots. This architecture balances throughput (parallel filtering/scoring), fairness (multiple queue levels with backoff), and extensibility (plugin framework with 12 extension points).\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":7132,"cache_read_input_tokens":81380,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":7132},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"bda0f306-61cd-4537-858a-1cc0c5ba072d","uuid":"2188f153-c416-4169-b274-4281ec699097"}

assumed, it's added to cache with nodeName set\n- Real Pod in API server doesn't have nodeName yet (binding hasn't occurred)\n- Cache maintains assumedPods set and podState map tracking assumed pods and their deadlines\n- Deadlines allow cache to clean up stale assumed pods (prevents memory leaks if binding fails)\n\n**Node Information Management**\n- Cache.NodeInfo tracks pods, resources, and predicates on each node\n- Doubly-linked list of NodeInfo sorted by recency (head = most recent)\n- UpdateSnapshot() called at start of scheduling cycle creates point-in-time view\n- Generation numbers track changes, allowing incremental snapshot updates\n\n**Image States**\n- Tracks image pull latency and availability on nodes\n- Used by plugins like ImageLocality for scheduling decisions\n\n### CycleState Design\n\n**Thread-Safe Scheduling Context**\n- Each pod gets its own CycleState instance for a scheduling cycle\n- Backed by sync.Map for \"write once, read many\" optimization\n- Plugins can store intermediate results (e.g., PreFilter stores computed data read by Filter)\n- Allows zero-copy plugin communication\n\n**State Propagation**\n- PodsToActivateKey reserved key: Plugins can inject pods to be activated post-scheduling\n- SkipFilterPlugins, SkipScorePlugins: PreFilter/PreScore plugins can signal to skip coupled plugins\n- Plugin metrics flags: Controls per-cycle metrics recording\n\n### Multi-Profile Support\n\n**Scheduler Profiles**\n- Scheduler can run multiple scheduler profiles simultaneously\n- Each profile has own Framework, QueueSort, and plugin chain\n- Pods specify .spec.schedulerName to choose profile\n- Allows different scheduling logic for different workload types\n\n## Key Data Structures\n\n### ScheduleResult\n```go\ntype ScheduleResult struct {\n    SuggestedHost string           // Selected node name\n    EvaluatedNodes int             // Nodes evaluated in filtering + beyond\n    FeasibleNodes int              // Nodes that passed filtering\n    nominatingInfo *NominatingInfo // For preemption tracking\n}\n```\n\n### QueuedPodInfo\n```go\ntype QueuedPodInfo struct {\n    Pod                      *v1.Pod\n    Timestamp                time.Time     // When pod entered queue\n    UnschedulablePlugins     sets.Set[string]\n    Attempts                 int           // Scheduling attempts count\n    InitialAttemptTimestamp  *time.Time\n}\n```\n\n### FitError (Scheduling Failure)\n```go\ntype FitError struct {\n    Pod         *v1.Pod\n    NumAllNodes int\n    Diagnosis   Diagnosis\n}\n\ntype Diagnosis struct {\n    NodeToStatusMap map[string]*Status  // Per-node rejection reasons\n    PreFilterMsg    string\n    PostFilterMsg   string\n}\n```\n\n## Data Flow During Scheduling\n\n1. **Pod Arrival**: Pod added to queue via event handler\n2. **Pop Phase**: ScheduleOne pops next pod from queue\n3. **Framework Selection**: Find Framework matching pod's schedulerName\n4. **Snapshot**: Cache.UpdateSnapshot() creates point-in-time node view\n5. **PreFilter**: Plugins may narrow down candidate nodes\n6. **Filter**: Determine feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n7. **Score**: Rank feasible nodes (parallel execution)\n8. **Selection**: Pick best node\n9. **Assume**: Mark pod as running on node in cache\n10. **Reserve**: Plugins update internal state\n11. **Permit**: Final gate; can delay or reject\n12. **Bind (async)**: Wait for permits, run PreBind plugins, call Bind plugins, run PostBind\n13. **Cleanup**: Mark pod as truly scheduled or requeue if binding failed\n\n## Failure Handling\n\n**Scheduling Cycle Failure** → Handled by FailureHandler\n- PostFilterPlugins run (e.g., preemption to free up resources)\n- Pod moved to backoffQ with exponential backoff\n- Will retry after backoff expires or cluster event occurs\n\n**Binding Cycle Failure** → Handled by handleBindingCycleError\n- Called if PreBind, Bind, or PostBind plugins fail\n- Reserve plugins' Unreserve methods called to clean up\n- assumed pod forgotten from cache\n- Pod requeued (triggers event-based requeue or backoff)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe Kubernetes scheduler implements a sophisticated two-phase lock-free scheduling architecture using a plugin framework. Pods are sorted via PriorityQueue, processed through a snapshot of cluster state, evaluated by parallel filter/score plugins, and speculatively assumed to run on selected nodes. The binding phase then asynchronously confirms the scheduling decision. The design enables multiple scheduling profiles, efficient event-driven pod requeuing via queueing hints, and extensibility through plugin interfaces at twelve extension points. CycleState provides thread-safe temporary state sharing between plugins, while the cache maintains node information with generation tracking for efficient incremental snapshots. This architecture balances throughput (parallel filtering/scoring), fairness (multiple queue levels with backoff), and extensibility (plugin framework with 12 extension points).\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
